  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_110489253" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110489253" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54697-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353271036p2/54697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110489253?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/54697-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 038001002x" href="/book/show/1846360.Call_It_Sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=social-crit">social-crit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=america-fuck-yeah">america-fuck-yeah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=fictions-of-the-big-it">fictions-of-the-big-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=put-aside">put-aside</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110489253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5401467180319832540">It's sort of like Stephen Dedalus as a 7 year old Austrian Jewish immigrant to New York city in the fresh turn of the 20th Century. <br/><br/>The first hundred plus pages got me going, but I've got to knock down a star for it's convoluted rendering of convoluted syntax. Really driving me nuts. I don't think Roth has to make it clearer, but he has got to render pidgin English just a little more palatable. Otherwise, it's like I get it, I get it, they're little kids in a foreign land without much schooling.</span>
  <span id="freeText5401467180319832540" style="display:none">It's sort of like Stephen Dedalus as a 7 year old Austrian Jewish immigrant to New York city in the fresh turn of the 20th Century. <br /><br />The first hundred plus pages got me going, but I've got to knock down a star for it's convoluted rendering of convoluted syntax. Really driving me nuts. I don't think Roth has to make it clearer, but he has got to render pidgin English just a little more palatable. Otherwise, it's like I get it, I get it, they're little kids in a foreign land without much schooling...a bit of overkill.<br /><br />The prose itself is really, really finely drawn...There's some touches of Whitman in there, amid the quasi-socialist realism. Roth does love the ugly, lovely place in some humanistic way. He can draw a character like none other- David's father and mother breath and sweat and curse and ruminate directly before your eyes. Vivid.<br /><br />It's hard to handle the grotesque well, too; it lends itself to ridiculousness and unintentional self-parody very easily. Few writers I've seen really know how to use it to its full advantage. Roth NAILS it. Everybloodybody's a screaming, resentful, masochistic, maudlin, nervous wreck...and the weather sucks and the streets are ominous and dirty and alien...powerfully effecting stuff.<br /><br />I love how it's kind of a lost classic, too. Lauded and forgotten almost simultaneously when it was released, a couple of critics picked up on it (I think it was Fielder and Trilling, but I might be wrong) and championed it and now it might be considered a minor masterpiece. <br /><br />Apparently the writing of it shook his 28 year old psyche enough for him to move to upstate New York and run a farm or something and have writer's block for twenty or thirty years until he came back with a trilogy of massive, 500 page tomes. Gotta respect that kind of toil, on both ends....</span>
  <a data-text-id="5401467180319832540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_103209042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103209042" />
    <a title="Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1701079-alan"><img alt="Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298403409p2/1701079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103209042?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alan" href="/user/show/1701079-alan">Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312424121" href="/book/show/46950.Call_It_Sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103209042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10727891669503031770">OK, I'm going to go for it this time. First of all I started out liking the book but after about 80 pages lost interest. And in fact I stopped reading twice before finally deciding to finish it. While some of the writing is gorgeous, I found much of the book unreadable and often felt like tearing out page after page of the idiomatic dialogue which, I had to read out loud to get any sense of what was going on. And then realizing that knowing what was being said didn't really matter in the end. I </span>
  <span id="freeText10727891669503031770" style="display:none">OK, I'm going to go for it this time. First of all I started out liking the book but after about 80 pages lost interest. And in fact I stopped reading twice before finally deciding to finish it. While some of the writing is gorgeous, I found much of the book unreadable and often felt like tearing out page after page of the idiomatic dialogue which, I had to read out loud to get any sense of what was going on. And then realizing that knowing what was being said didn't really matter in the end. I mean how many of these little asides did one need to get a sense of what this child and his family were about. And in the end did we really know them? <br /><br />What we seem to have is a really good short story, wrapped up in a really lousy novel. Good Grief! Charley Brown, what was that entire last chapter about. All that to get to the last sentence? Was that really necessary? Roth evidently decided to throw everything he ever thought about into writing this opus. Needed a good editor.....</span>
  <a data-text-id="10727891669503031770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_370372763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/370372763" />
    <a title="Emi Bevacqua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43247-emi-bevacqua"><img alt="Emi Bevacqua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175199318p2/43247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/370372763?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emi Bevacqua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emi Bevacqua" href="/user/show/43247-emi-bevacqua">Emi Bevacqua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer370372763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6417059582831435052">While I respect this as a historic classic, I can't say it was a pleasure for me to read. The first 400 pages I was dreading some kind of violent abuse against the main character, little David Schearl, a Jewish immigrant in New York's lower east side from eastern Europe. At first I suspected David's angry volatile unstable father, then the father's slimy work friend, and then a series of vile neighborhood punks, but again and again and again nothing happened aside from an agonizing building of t</span>
  <span id="freeText6417059582831435052" style="display:none">While I respect this as a historic classic, I can't say it was a pleasure for me to read. The first 400 pages I was dreading some kind of violent abuse against the main character, little David Schearl, a Jewish immigrant in New York's lower east side from eastern Europe. At first I suspected David's angry volatile unstable father, then the father's slimy work friend, and then a series of vile neighborhood punks, but again and again and again nothing happened aside from an agonizing building of tension. <br /><br />Conversely then, the final forty pages are filled with a non-stop series of hyper-manic vulgarities, action pace ramped up to max velocity, all alongside a constant barrage of multi-lingual "psycho-narration". Finally finished, I feel battered. The part I enjoyed the most is the Afterward. If I had a deeper grasp of the differences between Yiddish and Hebrew (and Ashkanazi vs Aramaic influences), I suppose this would have been a more entertaining read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6417059582831435052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t2xfI1yv+THaT1ochUT88Iao3uuAqvhrKIl9kSh8mTwTOdeuTRWhYZWe24RPkQfGpo9kNjqKxuU2yTK1Izs0ww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tGSbvi3KFwdX4A7n08Xk0tvq6uLs7Vps+ODIletwbXsQMRMzPHBPVxgxj38ZEB/k+81QP1bNZOLmoIex4DfAhA==')})
  }
